## Page 131

Con Cárdenas, sobre la Rica de

Bajo le Sigmo De

POR ROBERTO BLANCO MOHENO

La noche anterior a mi salida de Chi-

huahua,

cuando

comentaba con Javier

Palacio el horror de aquella situación, la

imposibilidad de dejar de ser "peripa-

tético" ante el vicio y el crimen herma-

nados para robar a un pueblo, la dolo

rosa necesidad de desafinar con amargas

verdades cuando todo el periodismo na-

cional forma el coro de las alabanzas,

una voz quenda me dijo, desde iléxico:

-Legó un telegrama del general

Cárdenas.

¡Dios! No cabe duda de que en la

vida existen las compensaciones. Porque

tenía en las manos, todavía, el olo mai-

dito de la prisión en que se mueren to

dos los días Ríos, Cardona y Rodriguez

F.; porque la crónica indignación se me

hacía un pozo doloroso ante la miseria

indescriptible de aquella buena gente, y

el valor sacrificado de los estudiantes,

Biazer Moneno

à da salerminable soledad del yermo de

Chihuabua, donde no viven ni

Siquiera

lagartijas. El nombre de Cárdenas, egoistamente, me hace olvidar, por

un momento no más, la rabia impotente que me muerde el alma. Se

me permitiri -lo permitirá usted. Pepe Pagés decir que al escu-

char el texto de ese telegrama siento las entrañas todas del alma

lavadas y hallo, en un camino a cada dia más duro, nuevas fuerzas

nacidas directamente de la mano de ese hombre maravilloso que es

don Lázaro. Si don Lázaro se pincha un dedo -jo digo con el mismo

derecho, y el mismo fervor, con que be dicho sobre el algunas inevi-

tables amargas verdades de ese dedo no sale sangre... ¡sale Mé

Xico!

Haría un mes que había mandado un mensaje a Ciudad Alta-

mirano, uno de los centros vitales de la Comisión del Balsas, dicién-

dole a Cárdenas que si era todavía oportuno, me gustaria conocer la

verdadera situación de la zona guerrerense y michoacana afectada por

los recientes temblores para ver la manera de hacer llegar al Presi-

dente López Mateos, paño de todas las lágrimas, las necesidades que

los señores gobernadores tienen la costumbre de no ver, ciegos casi

todos a puro egoismo. Cuando pasaron las semanas y de Ciudad Al-

tamirano nada llegó, sentí un poco de mordedura del despecho. Es

cierto que he dicho en estas páginas mi condena del a CCI y de sus

dirigentes comunistas -aunque no llegé a insultarlos como los pro

pios campesinos de esa Central hace unos días, en que los echaron

ignominiosamente; es verdad que acudí a dos reuniones de los diri-

gentes del Movimiento de Liberación Nacional, entre los cuales desta

caban Cuaubtémoc Cárdenas, Alonso y González Pedrero, y que me

retiré indignado ante la absurda postura, la inmovilidad y hasta la

cobardía que encontré: s algo más grave: tuve necesidad, en mi libro

"'El Cardenismo", de ahondar en algunas cosas que forzosamente do

lieron al gran michoacano. Pero no queria, no podía creer que el

Expropiador del Petróleo, el padre agrarista, el campeón del Derecho

Internacional sufriera la mezquina enfermedad que padecen nuestros

intelectuales rojos. ¿Si hay un hombre al que nunca debe llamársele

intelectual, dado el giro que la palabrita

ba tomado de quienes así

se llaman, ese hombre es Cárdenas! Y ahora escuchaba el texto

del mensaje que muy poco después iba a revelarme la grandeza de

México y la miseria de México, toda la enorme y dolorosa paradoja

que es este formidable pais: "Recibi con enorme retraso tu mensaje

porque no esture aqui. Serás bienvenido cuando quieras!.

No quie

ro, Pepe Pagés, aumento de sueldo: ¡ya estoy pagado lo suficiente!

corazón de esta desolada región, de pobreza subhumana, sin recursos,

pues si bien es cierto que "no bay tierra inala con agua" aquí no hay

tierra, sino tequesquite, piedra, tepetate, erosión, se levanta un pue

blito viejo en su anónimo dolor, en su hambre de siglos: se llamaba

Mariscala de Iturbide.

Algo ha ganado, en un sentido moral, porque

a la fecha se llama Mariscala de Juárez. El que escribe confiesal que

nunca habia oido hablar de este pueblo. Y junto al caserío miserable

veo desde el avión que conduce magistralmente el capitán Rufino! Sal-

gado una magnífica pista de aterrizaje. Y distingo, desde el aire,

una figura roqueña, hecha de esta misma tierra pobre, que hace un

alto pequeno en su trabajo de siempre para correrme una cortesia

meacanisima.

-Mira — digo a mi hijo Carlos a quien he traido porque considero

que ver trabajar a Cárdenas entre

el pueblo es la más alta lección

que puede recibir un joven alli está el general A su edad, mor.

diendo los setenta años, con su famo, su levendo y su significación,

este hombre podria estar recostado tranquitamente en el seno de la

Historia. Podría tener negocios enormes y dedicar sus horas ali pia-

cer y a la intrigo, dedicaciones ex-presidenciales por excelencia.

Se

levanto a las cinco de la mañana y suelen darle las doce de la noche

pegado al trabajo. Es preciso, muchacho, que comprendas el privile-

gio de que gozas.

Esta tu visita tiene la misma significación que si,

por lin malagro, estuvieras llegando al campamento de José Maria Mo-

relos o a la oficina errante de Benito Juárez...

Un abrazo y sin más transición los vips echan a andar rumbo al

poblado, en una de cuyas casas está instaiada la oficina. del Vocal

Ejecutivo.

Mientras despacha algunos radios, pues aquino bay te

legrafo, y atiende a unos campesinos de un pueblo que en esta zona

al parecér maldita lleva el nombre absurdo de "La Inspiración". yo

charlo con los ingenieros Lastari, Residente de la zona; Valdés AJ-

varez, Director de Comunicaciones y Urbanismo: Guillermo Soto, Sub

director; Jaime Traslosheros, Obras Hidráulicas, y Luis Suárez Fer-

nández, encargado de investigaciones economicas Estos hombres

eternos pioneros,

duros trabajadores que construyen México y su

grandeza, cuya misión terrible pero satisfactoria y bella consisté en

irse de los lugares cuando los lugares se han hecho habitables v. tie

nen ya caminos, y agua potable, y electricidad y. sobre todo, escuelas,

tienen la vena jocunda y la paciencia larga. Legaron aquí cuando la

Alta Mixteca no era sino una enorme tragedia sin caminos, ni luz, ni

comida siquiera. Traian dinero en los boisillos, pero pasaban hambre,

porque en esto región, donde miles y miles de mezanos viven -¿vi-

ven?- en la más terrible miseria, los frijoles, liase bien, los frijples

son un lijo. Nadie conoce aqui la leche y cuando recogen un huevo

de la gallina ranchera que algunos "ricos" tienen, ese huevo no es

comido por ellos, sino que sirve de moneda suprema para el inter-

cambio de pequeñas mercancías.

Y sin embargo, frente a esta miseria, no he sentido ni por un

momento la indignación, la rebeldía que me mordió en Chihuahua,

porque lo terrible -con serlo no es que una zona sea miserable,

aunque desde luego el hombre tiene la obligación de luchar contra

lo que los señores curas de la región llaman "la roluntad de Dios"

sino que donde hay riquezas, como en Chihuahua. la traición, 'el robo,

el crimen, presiden todas las cosas. Aqui se lucha por ayudar all in-

feliz mixteco, que a pesar de tener hambre de siglos - los ingenieros

me han dicho que pesos que en otras regiones son movidos fácilmente

por dos hombres aqui requieren seis es un indio vivaz en cuyas

comunidades el alcoholismo crónico -la verdadera enfermedad in-

dígena, una enfermedad inoculada por los traficantes mestizos y blán-

cos, no alcanza las proporciones espantables de Chiapas o Yucatán.

Don Lázaro me recibe en su oficina destartalada:

-Te felicito por las denuncias que haces ante el señor paperi

dente de la República en beneficio del pueblo explorado. Pero quise

que vinieras para que les lu autoridad moros en reconocer que no

todo es malo: podrás per cómo el gobierno federal. Bajo la dirección

P.ão line Matcos, lucha por el pretendido terion

МАСКОЙ ИЛН

1.

Background.

a. LIHUFF (Identity l) was founded in 1953 by a group of Mexican

businessmen to spread the principles of free enterprise and private initiative.

Since then, it has established numerous influential contacts and relationships

and engaged in a number of anti-Communist and other activities. It has neld

meetings of various types and congresses, in which the dangers of Communism

was the central theme; it has published books, pamphlets, and newsletters on

Communism as well as the dangers of economic socialismift has organized a

student group (Identity 2) It has established and maintained Latin American

contacts in the student and economic/business fields; it has engaged in cou-

siderable press placement on various matters involving private initiative and

(continued)

A. Right hand side (u/s/c)

B. Identities (u/s/c)

HMMA 23708

the Communisi threat; and it has accumulated a file of basie data on events and

individuals revolving about Communiem and Socialism that would be difficult for

any private Mexican group to duplicate.

This is quite aside from the many

individuals, such as LICHANT,, who have gravitated to LIHUFF and present

various types of capabilities in the press, publishing, and similar fielde.]

b. LIHUFF and its sponsors are considered in terms of the Mexican

scene as extreme right-wing conservatives; however, on the PBPRIME scene

they would be considered more as cent.ists. The importance of such a group,

vocal and combative, existing in Mexico, is nor in absolute terms but in relative

terms. As is known by Headquarters, the ruling Partido Revolucionario

Institucional (PRI) party is basically a delicate reflector of the many political

currente and presgures that exist in Mexico. In elections, appointments and

decisions, the PRI cabal weighs very carefully all political equities. If only the

extreme leftists are vocal and active, then the decisions tend to be weighted

in their favor and oriented toward their viewpoint. In so many words, in order

to keep some kind d counterbalance, even though tending towards extremes,

the fight must be as vocal and active ag the left. Essentially, this is where

the Station sees the value of the LIHUFF mechanism. It does not expect Mexico

ever to revert to the littuff philosophy or objectives en toto or even to any

very great degree; it does expect LIHUFF to exercise an influence and restraint

on Mexico succumbing to the pressures and demands of the far left. Unless

some few like LIHUFF/2'and Miguel ALEMAN Valdes were active through

organizations of their type, the political center of gravity would move further

towards the far left unchecked and further than ODYOKE policy would care *

see it. This is the unique and specific value that this Station has seen, and

continues to see, in the LIHUFF activity.

C.

In mid-1960, on the strensth of a LHUFF/2 contact with HBFINCH,

the Chief HBFINCH (Mexico) requested the Station to consider support of the

WHUFF activity. A check with Headquarters indicated that KUBARK had been

providing some support to HUFF through Identify

"3 "but inasmuch as ldentity

had died shortly before, the Station was asked by Headquarters to pick up the

funding. The Station funding initially was directed to Identity'?, the major.

regular publication of LIHUFF. A project was submitted by the Station in

reference C, but reference D indicated che project had been disapproved in the

form submitted, that support to Identfy should be discontinued, and that

instead, the Station funds should be applied to the student activity (Identity 2) MuNo

on a spot assistance basis. This was done with PBPRIME business associates

of LIHUFF/1 picking up the cost of Identity ' some $1, 200 (US) per month.

At the present time, therefore, Station expenditures are confined to LIHUFF/1

salary ($500 per month) and $500 per month to Identity 8. At this juncture

., the LIHUFF activity is costing $12, OU0 per year.

The Station, however, retains access to the full range of the LIHUFF mechanism

and potential.

2. Target.

The major target insofar a KUBARK funding is concerned is the

student field through Identity 2.

As is obvious, however, the LIHUFF mechaniem

is available and used for other activities as well. An example is the Identity

book by LICHANT/l and the reference D request for another LICHANT/1

publication on Cuban refugees. LIHUFF/1 and LIHUFF/2 increasingly provide

disseminable intelligence reports on political and student matters gathered

from their wide range of contacts. This is quite aside from a great deal of

opezational information of value to the Station which does not merit dissemination.

3. Control.

Station access to, and control of, this activity depends primarily on

the relationship of LIHUFF/1 with LIHUFF/2. Precisely what percentage of

income KUBARK is providing le the LIHUFF somplex is unknown lo the Stationi

however, it is known that PBPRIME bueinees men are underwriting Identity 1 '7

to the extent of $1200 (US) per month.

The circulars and other acuvities

sustained by LIHUFF must involve, conservatively, another $1200 (US) per

month

The $500 (US) per month funded to LIHUFF by the Station, while

maintaining access and certainly providing useful support to LIHUFF in the

student field, cannot be considered control insurance in this situalion.

Essentially, Station funds assure access for LIHUFF/1 to LIHUFF/2 on LIHUFE

matters and, with this entree, LIHUFF,l on the strength of their personal

relationship provides the control factor. Basically, the control factor is

probably guaranteed more by the personal relationship than the lunds. In any

event, the control over miHUff activities 1s not absolute and, even giver

complete funding of LIHUFF by KUBARK, would not be absolute. Possibly,

it could be improved a little more with some more funde, but nor much.

This is because LIHUFF R is successful, prominent, capable and involved with

too many other prominent people and events on his own to ever have any single :

individual or entity dictate bis activities, attitudes, and so on. He i responsive

to Station requirements on the use of Station funde and even seeks advice on

other LIHUFF activities not funded by the Station, What he is not readily

responsive to is detailed written reporting. He will give oral reports and

some written reports. Part of the problem in this regard undoubtedly is that

he is involved in so many activities that he finds it difficult to find the time.

For Station purposes in this particular program, the control is less than ideal

but certainly adequate for getting things done in the areas desired since there

is little question about his motivation and ability.

Jucke

Relationship to Other Projects.

Миль.

a. LICOAX: As indicated in reference B, both Project LICOAX and

Identity t are operating in UNAM, a university of upwards of 80,000 students.

Thus far, there has been no problem of conflict since one is working the

Catholic side of the street and the other, the so-called "independente" -- and

there is still plenty of room for both to operate. In this connection, it should

be noted that a great deal of LIHUFF student effort is devoted to several

universities outside Mexico City; in other words, the UNAM is just one aspect.

b. LISIREN: This project is concerned with a mass propaganda

approach to Communism in Mexico. It is headed by a group ol businessmen

known as Identity o.

The only relationship between LIHUFF and LISIREN is

in the fact that four of the members of Identity o are members of LIHUFF's

twenty-gix man "Bard of Directors". This does not necessarily mean an

interlocking directorate between the two projects as indicated in previous Head.

quarters correspondence, since, as in many similar activities in the PEPRIME,

individuals interested in civic or outside activities of this nature are frequently

tapped to serve in multiple assignments of this nature. At this juncture, with

LIHUFF concentrating on student activities in selected bigger universities, it

is not believed that there is any particular relationship of operational relevance

or import between these two instrumentalities. There are just four men

common to both boards.

c. LILISP/C: Since LILISP/C is a national student organization,

stressing student affairs in the interior of Mexico, obviously LIHUFF and

LILISP/C are working in the same general field in niversities outside Mexico

City. However, in the particular universities in which LIHUFF is concentrating

its efforts, this can be a complementary relationship since WHUFF can work in

much more depth in these universities than can LILISP/C and can affiliate its

groups to the LILISP/C national student confederation which is the only one now

generally recognized in Mexico. LILISP/C, as a national student confederation,

obviously can only spend very limited time on any single university or situation.

completed the printing of the book. Initial distribution is proceeding according

to the plan outlined in reference H. This Station expects to have 5,000 copies

of the book via air shipment from

for distribution by 20 June.

At that point, the Station will start moving copies of the book in small lots

long

through mailing and certain individuals to influential people, institutions, and

c. In short, as may be gathered from the present dispatch and

previous dispatches cited, the Station believes LIHUFF is doing a unique and

effective job in not only the student field but others as well.

Security.

AJa

Ther have been no security problems which have come to the

attention of the Station in connection with this activity. Both LIHUFF/1 and -

LIHUFF/2 have been, to the Station's inowledge, quite discreet about their

LIHUFF relationships. In view of the nature of the LIHUFF grap, there has

been no curiosity about the source of funds contributed by the Station. She

question of the LIHUFF and LISIREN activities croseing (due to common members

on their bard of directors) has never arisen in any context known tothe Station.

outline submitted by reference C would be the following:

(1) To alter the objectives to (a) supporting a student movement

(no Pu yet)

There are no particular proclems with this project except

those involving funds.

Thus far, LIHUFF/1 and LIHUFF/2 have found it pos-

sible to underrite other activities, such as IDATITY-6 and various aspects

of student undertakings, through ad hoc donations usually from PBRIE bus1-

ness interests in Mexio. However,

this does not lend Itselt to continuity

of effort and planning on anything but a short rance basis for obvious rea-

There is some competition between Froject LIHUFF and Project

LICOAX in UNAN that thus

far has been compatible.

Essentially, the forcer

works the Catholle side of the street and the latter, the so-called "inde-

pendent" side.

There has been plenty for each to do at UNAil up to this point.

The only reason this is pointed out 1s that at some time in the future this

could take a twist where a problem could come into existence, but not jet.

as it has in recent months; that 15, to aroride sunds for specified activi

ties in the four universities in which DENIT-l is now working based on

whatever priorities seen to exist at the time. ImuRo

tions are maintained by IDENTITY-1 in El Salvador, Panama, Peru, Chile, Uru-

guay, Venezuela and Colombia.

This 1s not being funded by the Station, but

it will receive the IDONTITY-l representatives reports on his trip.

LHUFF - Quarterly Progress Report (December 1963; January, February 1964)

Ref:

A. INMA 22575 of 6 December 1963

B. EMMA 22550 of 3 December 1963

•C. DIR 99100 of 4 February 1964

- D. DIR 45153 of 27 October 1962

- E. RYBAT ENMS 2530 of 15 August 1962

I. BACKGROUND:

Reference E advised the Station that for several years a grip, beaded

by the late Benry Hélland (formerly Assistant Secretary of State for Inter-

American Affairs) had been helping LTHUFP/2, particularly with a subsidy to

assist in the publication of the right-wing economics publication which he

edits.

2.

Reference D approved of a Station subsidy of $15,000 pesos ($1, 200.00

U.S, dollars) monthly to be given to LIHUFF/2 for this same publication.

3. The Mesco City Station's views on this publication and other aspects

of the LIEUFF operation were reported in reference B of 3 December 1963 - and

these views are still valid at the Station. In particular, paragraph 3 of

reference B gives the beckground an how the Mexico City Station becane Involved

In the subsidy to this very conservative and right wing economic publication.

or conservative, political groups in Mexico. The Union Macional Sinarguista

Embassy in Mexico and pretended to be interested in visas to go to this Congress

and made rcmarks about this Communist Congress.

III. PROBLEMS:

9. In view of the lack of formalized status and dependence upon O0A funds!

for financing, the principal problem has been to find cleared businessmen

(Americans) to whom the Station could appeal for continued financial support of

the publication and some student activities of the LIHUFF groupe.

IV. PLANS:

10. The Station plans to abide by reference C Insofar as expenditures from

Station funds are concerned.

Any other financial support will of necessity have

to come from interested U.S. businessmen.

11. The Station plans to coutinue to use the M.U.R.0, student organization

BB a vIgorous and

"shock troop" type group in support of Station and KUBARK

student anti-Commnist objectives. The M.U.R.0. group will also continue to

be used as sources of information of interest on University activities..

12.

The Mexico CIty Station can also use LIHUFT/2 as & writer (who can on his

own get articles in "El Valversal" and "Excelsior", Mexico's two bizgest and best

nevspapers). His use will be restricted to strongly anti-Communist, anti-

Soviet articles.

V. SECURITY:

13.. There have been no security problems during this period. Only LLHUFT/1

18 aare of ODYOKE Involvement;

LTHUFF/2 and others believe businessnen are

still the sources of funde and guidances.

17. As stated in paragraph 10 above, the Station plans henceforth to spend:

$500 (dollars) monthly to support student activities, primarily

M.V.R.0.; and

b. $500 (dollars) monthly as the salary to IlHUFT/1.

15. Any other monies LIHUFF gets as a result of Station actions will come

from support of U.S. business contacte of the Station.
